    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="7015012a2bda4fb18474f0eb0ff48d12">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '0cd18777-084d-40d0-98a1-3aa9e1f81c4e'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

                     <p>Tianjin Key Laboratory of Functional Crystal Materials, Institute of Functional Crystal, College of Material Science and Engineering, Tianjin University of Technology, Tianjin, 300384 China</p><a class="moreInfoLink" href="/authored-by/Hu/Zhanggui">Search for more papers by this author</a></div></span><span class="accordion-tabbed__tab-mobile  accordion__closed"><a href="/authored-by/Long/Zhen" class="author-name accordion-tabbed__control" data-id="a18" data-db-target-for="a18" aria-controls="a18" aria-haspopup="true" id="a18_Ctrl" role="button"><span>Zhen Long<i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-mail_outline"></i></span><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-section_arrow_d"></i></a><span class="comma-separator">,&nbsp;</span><div class="author-info accordion-tabbed__content" data-db-target-of="a18" aria-labelledby="a18_Ctrl" role="region" id="a18">

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d169048105" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>Rapid capacity fading and structural collapse, along with other deep-rooted challenges in the high-voltage region, are insufficient to meet the requirements for commercial applications of O3-type layered cathodes. Hereby, rare earth metal (RE) within the IIIB group are utilized as the robust dopants for O3-NaNi<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (NFM) to achieve the purpose of reconstructing the crystal lattice and regulating the interlayer structure. The inactive RE<sup>3+</sup> acts as a pillar, reinforces the TMO<sub>6</sub> octahedron, and broadens the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion layer in the configuration of O-Na-O-TM (RE)-O-Na-O, giving rise to the enhanced crystal stability and accelerating the transmission of sodium ions. More impressively, the scandium incorporation is working as a “vitamin” that improves Ni/Fe redox reversibility, alleviating the irreversible P3-O3’-P3’ phase transformation and further restraining the disordered Fe migration into the neighboring Na layer, which is firmly validated by in situ X-ray diffraction coupled with the synchrotron X-ray absorption spectroscopy. Consequently, the as-designed NFM-Sc exhibits impressive rate capability (82.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 10 C) and excellent cycle stability with 80.2% capacity retention after 500 cycles at the high voltage of 4.2&nbsp;V. Given this, the elaborate work may shed new insight into the operational mechanism of rare metal through strategically regulating the structure for sodium-ion batteries.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202402398-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202402398-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>In the past few decades, lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have dominated the global market for electronic products and electric vehicles because of the advantages of high energy density and long-lasting cycle life.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0001_R_d169048048e593" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Science">1</a>-<a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0004_R_d169048048e593" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Renewables">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Unfortunately, the shortage of lithium resources has obstacles to LIBs expansion to a broader scale of application, especially in the field of large-scale energy storage applications. Intensive attention was attracted to sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) as a promising candidate due to the abundant resources and cost efficiency of sodium. Thereinto, O3-type layered transition metal oxides with a formula of Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>TMO<sub>2</sub> (<i>x</i> &lt; 0.7), benefited from their considerably reversible capacity and tunable composition, are utilized as favored cathode materials for high-energy-density SIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0005_R_d169048048e606" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">5</a>-<a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0007_R_d169048048e606" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Renewables">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Among the various candidates, cobalt-free O3-NaNi<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (NFM) is considered as one of the most promising Ni-Fe-Mn based cathodes, first explored by Johnson et al,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0008_R_d169048048e621" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Electrochem. Commun.">8</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> which could deliver an appreciable reversible capacity of 130&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> within a voltage of 2.0–4.0&nbsp;V and especially possesses a comparatively simple phase transformation (O3-P3-O3) and air stability, distinguishing it from representative NaNi<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> in the Ni-Mn base O3-type cathodes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0009_R_d169048048e636" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Adv. Energy Mater.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Simultaneously, the prominent cost-competitive and environmentally friendliness due to the usage of manganese and iron elements make it possible for practical application as commercial energy storage materials.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0010_R_d169048048e641" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - J. Electrochem. Soc.">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Nevertheless, NFM should strive to augment its reversible capacity, like broadening the voltage range, because the current specific capacity below 4.0&nbsp;V is insufficient to fulfill the requirement for high-energy-density batteries.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0011_R_d169048048e646" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Chem. Mater.">11</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, it usually undergoes the additional irreversible P3-O3’-P3’ monoclinic phase transitions when the cut-off voltage rises to 4.2&nbsp;V, resulting in the migration of transition metal ions with sharp distorted lattice volume and rapid capacity fading during the cycling process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0012_R_d169048048e652" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Chem. Mater.">12</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Furthermore, the limited interlayer structure for O3-phase and severe parasitic side reactions at the internal electrode/electrolyte interface, which may further contribute to the unsatisfactory rate capability and undesired cycling stability, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0013_R_d169048048e657" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Adv. Energy Mater.">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Admittedly, most previously reported strategies have been devoted to addressing the bottleneck problems above, such as surface coatings, metal-ion doping into the bulk structure, and multiphase combination.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0014_R_d169048048e664" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Energy Storage Mater.">14</a>, <a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0015_R_d169048048e664" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Nat. Commun.">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In particular, cationic doping in bulk was corroborated as the most successful remedy to regulate the interlayer structure and inhibit harmful O-P phase evolutions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0016_R_d169048048e669" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Engl.">16</a>-<a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0018_R_d169048048e669" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Renewables">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In recent studies, extensive investigations on the working mechanism of cationic dopants by using Li,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0019_R_d169048048e674" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Adv. Energy Mater.">19</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Mg,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0020_R_d169048048e680" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Small">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> V,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0021_R_d169048048e685" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Energy Storage Mater.">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Ti,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0022_R_d169048048e691" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Al,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0023_R_d169048048e696" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - J. Phys. Chem. C">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Cu,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0024_R_d169048048e701" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Sci. Bull.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Zr,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0021_R_d169048048e707" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Energy Storage Mater.">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and Sn<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0025_R_d169048048e712" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - ACS Nano">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> are readily available. For example, Li-dopant could serve for O3-Na<sub>0.85</sub>Li<sub>0.1</sub>Ni<sub>0.175</sub>Mn<sub>0.525</sub>Fe<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> as the J-T distortion of Ni<sup>3+</sup> can be mitigated and unfavorable P3-P’3 phase transition can be effectively suppressed at high voltages (&gt; 4.2&nbsp;V vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0026_R_d169048048e735" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Chem">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Lately, Ti-substitution could greatly boost the structural stability for O3-NaNi<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> because of the suppressed irreversible P’3-O’3 phase transition in the high voltage regions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0022_R_d169048048e747" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Rare earth elements (RE) are widely acknowledged as vitamins for modern industry and are considered beneficial to LIBs and SIBs due to their excellent features such as high electric conductivity, large ionic radius, and high self-polarization ability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0027_R_d169048048e754" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - ACS Appl Mater Interfaces">27</a>, <a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0028_R_d169048048e754" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Engl.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Sc-doped NASICON Solid-state electrolytes have demonstrated superior Na-ion ionic conductivity and improved cycling performance, which account for the expansion of lattice volume in the rhombohedral phase and alterations in the lengths of the Na─O bond. In addition, it demonstrates that the incorporation of Lanthanum (La) and Yttrium (Y) elements, which possess high bond energy and a larger radius, could effectively expand the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion layer accompanied with the improved comprehensive electrochemical performance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0008_R_d169048048e761" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Electrochem. Commun.">8</a>, <a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0029_R_d169048048e761" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Energy Storage Mater.">29</a>, <a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0030_R_d169048048e761" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Nanoscale">30</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the underlying intrinsic working mechanism of RE-doping in layered cathodes remains poorly understood.</p>
         
         <p>In this work, taking NaNi<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> as the representative material, rationally incorporation with RE elements of Sc, Y, La from IIIB group to improve the high-voltage cyclic stability for O3-type layered oxides during (de)sodiation process in details. By systematically altering crystal interlayer structure, coordination environment, electronic state, and electrochemical performance, Scandium was proven to be the most effective candidate in optimizing crystal structure and functioning as an anticipated reversible Na<sup>+</sup> storage under the high-voltage region (≈4.2&nbsp;V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>). Combined with the analysis of ex situ synchrotron X-ray spectroscopy (XAS) and In situ X-ray diffraction (XRD), which are further utilized to reveal the redox reversibility of Ni/Fe and migrate irreversible migration through Fe<sup>4+</sup> couple with suppressed irreversible volume expansion/contraction by Sc modification. Moreover, a more stable layered structure for NFM-Sc has demonstrated the enhanced ion transfer kinetics, eases microcracking production, and hinders parasitic side reactions at the interface for long-term cycling. Eventually, under the influence of a restrained lattice phase transition and expended Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion layer spacing, NFM-Sc exhibits a superior long-term cycling stability of 80.2% after 500 cycles with significantly enhanced rate performance within the voltage range of 2.0–4.2&nbsp;V.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202402398-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202402398-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <p>The pristine O3-NFM and RE-doped samples were prepared by the coprecipitation and solid-state calcination method. The atomic compositions of all the final products were confirmed through inductively coupled plasma optical emission spectrometry (ICP-OES), as shown in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> (Supporting Information), well match with the target stoichiometry. As depicted in <b>Figure</b> <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section"><b>1</b>a</a>, the Powder X-ray diffraction (XRD) confirms that the main diffraction peaks are isostructure with α-NaFeO<sub>2</sub> (PDF# 54–0887) layered structure with R −3 m symmetry. Obviously, the newly appeared characteristic peak for NFM-La corresponds to the LaMnO3 phase (PDF# 86–1234), which is a common phenomenon for La<sup>3+</sup> doping in Mn-base layered cathodes. As a comparison of the (003) plane in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0001">1b</a>, the diffraction peaks were shifted toward a lower Bragg angle after RE doping, indicating RE elements were undoubtedly introduced into the crystal lattice and different levels of alteration interlayer structure based on the Bragg equation.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202402398-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/f9272f11-8200-4cd0-b6d3-793133366f2b/adfm202402398-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/f9272f11-8200-4cd0-b6d3-793133366f2b/adfm202402398-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/ed327975-9224-46ed-ba25-454e485664a6/adfm202402398-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/f9272f11-8200-4cd0-b6d3-793133366f2b/adfm202402398-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202402398-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202402398" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Powder XRD patterns of a) O3-NFM and RE (Sc, Y, and La) doped samples, b) magnified view of the (003) crystal face. c,d) Rietveld refinement patterns of the XRD data for NFM and NFM-Sc. e) the changes of lattice parameters <i>a</i> and <i>c</i> with doping Re elements. f) Schematic diagram of crystal structure from NFM to NFM-Sc. g) Ni K-edge XANES spectra for the powder NFM and NFM-Sc samples, h) EXAFS R space curve, and corresponding i) EXAFS WT images.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Besides, XRD Rietveld refinement analysis was applied to extrapolate the crystallographic parameters and atomic occupancies information following the incorporation of RE elements, as schematically performed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0001">1c,d</a>, Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> (Supporting Information). Meanwhile, the main lattice parameters of <i>a</i> value is decreased, <i>c</i> is enlarged after introducing the RE, as depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0001">1e</a>. This indicated that all the parts of the octahedral 3b site in the octahedron were successfully occupied by RE elements, resulting in the formation of the O3-NFM-RE solid solution. Additionally, the most significant factor is that the higher bond energy Sc-O (674.13&nbsp;kJ mol<sup>−1</sup>)and larger ionic radius of Sc<sup>3+</sup> (74.5 pm) doping into the configuration of O-Na-O-TM-O-Na-O along the <i>c</i>-axis, it would weaken the Na-O bond and enlarge spacings of Na layers, which is well consistent with Vegard's law.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0031_R_d169048048e863" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Engl.">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Consequently, the corresponding calculated results for interlayer structure are illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0001">1f</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information). The slab thickness of the TMO<sub>6</sub> octahedron is shrunk from 2.377 to 2.272 Å, while the spacing of the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion layer is broadened from 2.954 to 3.065 Å, further demonstrating the successful substitution of RE, which could further facilitate the enhancement of Na<sup>+</sup> storage properties and structure stability.</p>
         
         <p>The pre-edge peaks for Ni K-edge of the X-ray absorption near-edge structure spectra (XANES) of selected samples are illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0001">1g</a>, the slightly decreased intensity demonstrates that the lattice centrosymmetry is strengthened by the introduction of Sc. To further investigate the short-range local electron structure, the extended X-ray absorption fine structure (EXAFS) spectra were Fourier transformed (FT) magnitude to obtain the magnitude of R spacing, as depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0001">1h</a>. It is worth noting that the intensity of Ni-O and Ni-TM coordination shell for NFM-Sc is significantly higher than that in NFM, which can be ascribed to Sc doping caused lattice distortion. More considerably, an apparently longer Ni-O interatomic distance implies the reduced oxidation state of Ni and increased sodium storage resulted from Sc modification. Furthermore, the <i>k</i><sup>3</sup>-weighted magnitude to the wavelet transforms (WT) in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0001">1i</a> also suggests that the strengthened Ni coordination environment and emerged Ni-Sc scattering.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0032_R_d169048048e897" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Sci. Adv.">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Therefore, it can be concluded that the structure of the NiO<sub>6</sub> octahedron has been well improved due to the successfully introduced Sc<sup>3+</sup>, thereby greatly promoting robust structural and electrochemical properties.</p>
         
         <p>The evolutions of morphology and microstructure on RE-modified materials were characterized by field emission scanning electron microscopy (FE-SEM) and High-resolution transmission electron microscopy (HR-TEM). Noted that all the samples are the spheroid shape of large secondary particles, which are densely stacked by a great number of irregular primary nanoparticles (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information). As for the representative sample of NFM-Sc in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0002">2a,b</a>, exhibiting less surface residual alkali and more densely stacked secondary particles than NFM that may be beneficial to maintain the surface structure stability. In addition, HR-TEM and the relevant fast Fourier transform (FFT) images are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0002">2c</a>, which clearly reveal the typical layered hexagonal structure, and the width of ≈ 2.64 Å lattice space corresponds to the d-spacing values of the (006) plane with R −3 m spacing group. The energy dispersive spectroscopy (EDS) elementary mapping, as displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0002">2d</a>, indicates that Ni, Sc, Mn, and Fe elements are uniformly distributed in the NFM-Sc bulk particles.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202402398-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/69287ea9-1ffc-473a-aefe-d4630622df9b/adfm202402398-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/69287ea9-1ffc-473a-aefe-d4630622df9b/adfm202402398-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/535cd772-5b4f-4e6b-8674-12ececdc8bd7/adfm202402398-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/69287ea9-1ffc-473a-aefe-d4630622df9b/adfm202402398-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202402398-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202402398" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a,b) SEM images of NFM and NFM-Sc. c) HR-TEM pattern and corresponding FFT patterns of NFM-Sc. d) EDS mapping images of nickel, scandium, manganese, and iron elements distributed in NFM-Sc particles. e) sXAS spectra of Ni L-edge, Fe L-edge, Mn L-edge, f) XPS spectra of Sc 2p, g) O K-edge, and O 1s spectra for NFM and NFM-Sc samples.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Furtherly, soft X-ray absorption spectroscopy (sXAS) and X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) analyses were adopted to explore the evolution of surface valence state and electronic state upon the introduction of RE elements.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0033_R_d169048048e947" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Nat. Commun.">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0002">2e</a>, no obvious difference was observed in the peaks of the selected samples at the Mn L-edge, Fe L-edge, and Ni L-edge, indicating that it has no distinct change in valence states and basically maintained at +4, +3, and +2, respectively. Specifically, a higher intensity ratio of A<sub>2</sub>/A<sub>1</sub> represents the elevated oxidation state of transition metal.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0034_R_d169048048e960" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Note that, the intensity of peaks A<sub>2</sub> are noticeably decreased in sXAS of Mn/Fe/Ni L3-edge for NFM-Sc, implying oxidation state of the transition metal approached the standard valence state for O3-type cathodes, and demonstrating the electronic state to a more ideal condition could be adjusted by Sc-dopant. Moreover, new peaks located at ≈ 402&nbsp;eV were shown in the Sc 2p spectra of NFM-Sc (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0002">2f</a>), which corresponds to the binding energy value of the Sc<sup>3+</sup> ion. Apart from the valence state of transition metal, the local structure of surface O also deserves more attention. The significant differences were also noticed in the pre-edge regions of the O K-edge sXAS spectra (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0002">2g</a>), particularly the strengthened peaks at 531.7&nbsp;eV (blue region) in NFM-Sc compared to NFM, which means the higher Ni<sup>2+</sup> 3d-O 2p hybridization level and lower oxidation state of Ni. Meanwhile, the lattice oxygen for NFM-Sc of O 1s is located ≈529.0&nbsp;eV in XPS (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0002">2h</a>), which takes up a larger proportion than NFM, indicating that a more stable transition metal-oxygen bond is constructed. Besides, the peaks possessed 533.1&nbsp;eV for O <i>K</i>-edge and 532.0&nbsp;eV in O 1s generally represents the surface residual alkali, such as Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, and the reduced intensity of the above peaks indicates that intrinsic air sensitivity was reduced by Sc-incorporation and render the material more stable against exposure to air.</p>
         
         <p>The aforementioned discussions provide empirical evidence for effectively regulating interlayer structure, microstructure, and electronic state through RE doping; thereby, it is expected to substantially strengthen the cycling durability and kinetic performance of O3-type layered cathodes.</p>
         
         <p>The reconstructed structural traits of the Re-modified NFM discussed above would have an impact on the evolution of electrochemical performances. Therefore, the comprehensive and systematic electrochemical tests were performed on assembled coin-type half cells utilizing Na metal as an anode. The initial galvanostatic charge–discharge (GCD) curves at 0.1 C (1 C = 130&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>) are displayed in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0003">3a</a>; it is clear that RE-modified cathodes exhibit similar charge–discharge curves to that of the pristine but slightly reduced charge capacities, indicating no extra redox reaction caused by incorporated electrochemically inactive RE elements. Surprisingly, the initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) of the NFM-Sc, NFM-Y, and NFM-La are boosted from 84.90% to 88.26%, 87.36% and 87.12%, respectively. Furthermore, the discharge capacity of NFM-Sc and NFM-La are recorded as 156.1 and 155.5 mAh g<sup>−1,</sup> respectively, which is higher than that of NFM (154.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>), implying that RE-doping could facilitate the structural reversibility. The corresponding dQ/dV curves (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0003">3b</a>) were calculated to characterize the primary oxidation and reduction process within a voltage window of 2.0–4.2&nbsp;V. The first major redox peaks close to 3.0&nbsp;V (vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) represent the O3-P3 phase transition during the charge/discharge process. The polarization potential ΔE<sub>1</sub> of the RE-modified cathodes are decreased, which is 59.1&nbsp;mV for NFM-Sc in contrast to 201.4&nbsp;mV for NFM. Similarly, the second pair of redox peaks that are close to 4.0&nbsp;V exhibits a lower polarization potential ΔE<sub>2</sub> for the P3-O3’ phase transition. These results above suggest that the polarization was alleviated by RE incorporation, which obtained highly reversible electrochemical behaviors and reduced irreversible capacity loss during the Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction process.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202402398-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/70f5374c-4270-4f33-904b-5ecaae526b97/adfm202402398-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/70f5374c-4270-4f33-904b-5ecaae526b97/adfm202402398-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/15d0cfbe-5b10-498c-9deb-3381bd19c974/adfm202402398-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/70f5374c-4270-4f33-904b-5ecaae526b97/adfm202402398-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202402398-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202402398" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Initial GCD curves and b) corresponding dQ/dV profiles at 0.1 C. c) discharge curves at different current rates for NFM and NFM-Sc. d) NFM and NFM-Sc at 1&nbsp;C for 50 cycles. e) long-term cycling performance at 5 C for 500 cycles. Electrochemical performances of NFM-Sc||HC full-cell tested at 1.5–4.2&nbsp;V for f) first two charge–discharge curves at 0.1 C and g) circle stability at 1 C. h) Radar summary chart for comprehensive comparison performances of all-prepared cathodes.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Subsequently, the rate capabilities of the prepared samples at various ranging from 0.1 to 10 C were further compared, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0003">3c</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a> (Supporting Information). As observed, RE elements play a crucial role in the improvement of rate capability. Even tested at a high rate of 10 C, NFM-Sc, NFM-Y, and NFM-La still retain impressive capacities of 82.5, 74.5, and 63.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, in contrast to 60.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> for the pristine NFM. In other words, their capacity retention was ameliorated from 39.5% to 53.9%, 49.4%, and 40.9%, respectively, relative to 100-fold of the initial current density. Among them, the highest capacity retention and lowest voltage polarization are shown for NFM-Sc during various rate tests, and also exhibits better reversibility, as the capacity could recover back with little loss when the current density back to 0.1 C. It demonstrates that the Na<sup>+</sup> transport kinetics was accelerated due to extending the interlayer spacing of O-Na-O by introducing the Sc<sup>3+</sup>. Apart from the desirable improvement of rate performance by Sc-doping, the cycling performance tests were further evaluated. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0003">3d</a>, the first 50 cycles of charge/discharge profiles of NFM and NFM-Sc cathodes were compared at 1 C in the voltage range of 2.0–4.2&nbsp;V. Notably, the fast capacity/voltage fading was undergone by NFM at high cut-off voltage, which could be attributed to poor phase transition reversibility. As a result, the NFM electrode only retains a capacity of 105.2&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> after 50 cycles with 83.4% capacity retention. However, NFM-Sc maintained a reversible capacity of 119.6&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup>, coupled with a higher capacity retention of 91.0% under the same cycling condition. It implies that the introduction of Sc<sup>3+</sup> could effectively enhance the structure reversibility and prominently inhibit the fast capacity degradation and voltage fading for the NFM at high cut-off voltage as the number of cycles increases. Moreover, all the samples were further investigated for long-term cyclability at a higher rate of 5 C. As illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0003">3e</a>, an unstable cycle characterized by visible capacity deterioration for NFM, merely 61.8% of the initial capacity was retained with a prolonged cycle life up to 500 cycles. In contrast, the capacity retention values of RE-doped cathodes have been effectively improved that of NFM-Sc, NFM-Y, and NFM-La are 80.2%, 72.3%, and 65.3% after 500 cycles, respectively. Correspondingly, a stable CE close to 100% was exhibited by NFM-Sc, whereas the CE for NFM is frequent and highly variable, further suggesting the effectiveness and superiority of Sc-modification.</p>
         
         <p>Furthermore, to evaluate the potential of the obtained Sc-NFM cathode materials for practical utilization, coin-type sodium-ion full batteries are further assembled by coupling a reported hard carbon (HC) as the anode. In order to diminish the negative impact, a pre-sodiation process of 10 cycles was undergone by HC electrodes using Na metals as the counter electrode before actual use. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0003">3f</a> depicts the NFM-Sc||HC full cell that the similar GCD curves to NFM-Sc-half cell at 0.1 C, delivered an initial specific reversible capacity of 145.3&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> and CE of 77.21%, which are both slightly reduced due to end-of-discharge voltage being set at 1.5&nbsp;V to prevent Na metal precipitation. As the current is increased to 1 C, 80.8% of its initial capacity can be remained after 100 cycles, accompanied with an average coulombic efficiency close to 99% (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0003">3g</a>), demonstrating excellent cycling durability Above all, a radar summary chart was plotted to comprehensively and was systematically analyzed the properties of these RE-modification cathode materials, as revealed in the Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0003">3h</a>, in which a relatively regular pentagram of the as-designed Sc-doping strategy for NFM cathode achieves an excellent integrated performances.</p>
         
         <p>Given the significant impact of Sc-doping on the enhancement of comprehensive electrochemical performance, ex situ synchrotron X-ray absorption near-edge structure spectra (XANES) investigation is applied to understand the effect of Sc on transition metal redox behaviors and crystal structures during the Na<sup>+</sup> deintercalation process, as shown in <b>Figures</b> <a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0004">4a–c</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information). Regarding the electrochemically active elements, Ni/Fe K-edge spectra of NFM and NFM-Sc resemble those of NiO and Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, indicating that predominant oxidation states are the +2 and +3 for nickel ion and iron ion, agreeing well with the hXAS analysis in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0002">2e</a>. Upon the initial Na<sup>+</sup> ion extraction, ≈3&nbsp;eV was shifted toward higher energy for the Ni K-edge spectrum when selected samples were charged to 4.2&nbsp;V, suggesting the occurrence of an oxidation reaction involving Ni<sup>2+</sup>/Ni<sup>4+</sup>. When the Na<sup>+</sup> ion was fully inserted at the 2.0&nbsp;V discharging state, Ni K-edges recovered to their initial positions, indicating the high reversibility of Ni redox. Similarly, a shift of ≈2&nbsp;eV was observed for the Fe K-edge spectrum, which can be ascribed to Fe<sup>3+</sup>/Fe<sup>4+</sup> redox occurring during the charge/discharge process. Notably, the Ni absorption edge of NFM-Sc was collected at the discharged state, which is well-overlapped in a pristine position. In contrast to the slight skewing of NFM, implying the increased reversibility for the Ni redox and a modified local environment with Sc doping, ultimately resulting in a higher discharge capacity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0035_R_d169048048e1115" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - J. Power Sourc.">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, both the Fe K-edge peaks of selected samples failed to recover the pristine profile, indicating irreversible conversion of Fe<sup>4+</sup> back to Fe<sup>3+</sup> within the voltage range of 2.0–4.2&nbsp;V. However, the perfectly coincident Fe-O coordination shell and closer Fe-TM coordination shell of EXAFS intensity for NFM-Sc than NFM electrode, illustrating that incorporation of Sc helps alleviate the evolution of the local environment of iron. Simultaneously, the enhanced intensity of the pre-edge peak of NFM represents the existing Jahn-Teller active high-spin Fe<sup>4+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0036_R_d169048048e1127" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> It further demonstrates that the Fe coordination number was stabilized and coordination structure was prevented to distortion with Sc incorporation, and thus may restrain irreversible migration of Fe<sup>4+</sup> from transition metal layers (octahedral sites) to sodium ion layers.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202402398-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/e6c00e8e-76bf-4477-afa5-d3dd77765e4d/adfm202402398-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/e6c00e8e-76bf-4477-afa5-d3dd77765e4d/adfm202402398-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/81964ba2-f536-4be0-b483-30b6bfbea86f/adfm202402398-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/e6c00e8e-76bf-4477-afa5-d3dd77765e4d/adfm202402398-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202402398-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202402398" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a,b) Ex situ XANE spectra of NFM-Sc electrodes collected at different charge/discharge states. c) Ex situ EXAFS R-space curves of Fe K-edge for the samples. d) The Contour plots of (003) peaks collected from in situ XRD test during the initial charge/discharge process between the 2.0–4.2&nbsp;V. e) Schematic illustration of structural evolution during the first cycling for the O3-type cathodes. f-,g) The detailed changes of lattice parameters <i>a</i> and <i>c</i> of selected electrodes during the cycling process.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To systematically understand the relationship between the electrochemical properties and structure evolution, an in situ XRD test was conducted for the NFM and NFM-Sc cells cycled during the initial sodiation/desodiation process within 2.0–4.2&nbsp;V at 0.1 C, as shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a> (Supporting Information). With the beginning of Na<sup>+</sup> extraction and oxidation of transition metal ions in the charging process, the (00<i>l</i>) diffraction peaks were shifted toward a lower degree while the (10<i>l</i>) moved in the opposite direction, which means a solid solution process with the expanded <i>c</i>-axis and the shrunk <i>a</i>-axis along <i>a</i>-<i>b</i> plane. Once the voltage exceeded 3.05&nbsp;V, the main peak (003) was rapidly weakened and split into two parts: the original O3 phase and new P3 phase, illustrating the coexistence of the region of the O3-P3 phase. Subsequently, only the left-shifted single-phase solid solution process without any residual O3 phase means the O3-P3 phase transition is completely finish, as the voltage was increased to 4.0&nbsp;V. When the voltage was further increased from 4.0 to 4.2&nbsp;V, the P3 phase disappeared and only a continuously and drastic shift of the (003) peaks to a higher angle, it should be assigned to a monoclinic O3’ phase (space group C2/m) here in consistence with previous reports.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0037_R_d169048048e1179" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Adv. Energy Mater.">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Compared to an ideal hexagonal cell structure, the sharp distorted lattice with P3-O3’ phases evolution majorly originated from alleviated electrostatic repulsion of O-Na-O, which thanks to the enhanced TM-O orbital hybridization reduces the impact of pillar-effect. This strong interaction between adjacent TMO<sub>2</sub> layers leads to structural degradation and deficient electrochemical performances.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0038_R_d169048048e1187" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - ACS Nano">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the subsequent discharge process, the XRD pattern seems to exhibit a relatively opposite evolution compared to that observed during the charging process. However, the fact is that O3’ transforms to P3’ monoclinic phase and eventually returns back to the O3 phase.</p>
         
         <p>As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0004">4e</a>, both NFM and NFM-Sc experienced the asymmetric O3-P3-O3’-P3’-O3 phase transition sequence during the whole charge/discharge process. However, the unidentical phase transition behaviors of selected samples were evidenced by 2D contour plots of (003) diffraction peaks in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0004">4d</a>, which represents the change in the value of <i>c</i>-axis. On this basis the corresponding c/a axis lattice parameters were calculated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0004">4f,g</a>. Specifically, an obvious peak shift of 1.70° was observed by NFM during the P3→O3’ phase transition, corresponding to a shrinkage of 7.7% in the lattice <i>c</i>-axis and 6.7% in the lattice <i>a</i>-axis. Comparatively speaking, the smaller peak shift of 1.38° within P3→O3’ phase transformation for NFM-Sc, correlating to inhibited the reduced lattice values of <i>a/c</i> of 6.9%/6.3%, indicating the severe phase transition is noticeably mitigated with Sc-modification. Furthermore, before and after the P3-O3’-P3’ phase transition process, the comparison is that the peak shift of NFM is 0.24° while only 0.18° for NFM-Sc, which can be interpreted as the enhanced structure reversibility with the doped Sc. According to the results of ex situ XANE and in situ XRD, it confirmed that the function of Sc-dopant for NFM majorly is the improving the Ni/Fe redox reversibility and restraining irreversible migration of Fe<sup>4+</sup> couple with suppressed the irreversible phase transitions, and be expected to facilitate reversible Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion and alleviate the degraded crystallinity during long-term cycling.</p>
         
         <p>In order to further investigate the impedance information during the cycling process, electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) of the NFM and NFM-Sc electrodes was performed at open circuit potential (before the test) and the fully discharged state (after 100 cycles) at 1 C. As present in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0005">5a,b</a>, the Nyquist plots of uncycled samples primarily consist of a semicircle in the medium-high-frequency regions and then followed a straight line in the low-frequency region, which were regarded as the charge transfer impendence <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> and Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion impedance in Warburg region <i>W</i><sub>s</sub>. The difference is that a new semicircle appeared at high frequency, denoted as conductive interface impedance <i>R</i><sub>sf</sub>, due to the formation of the cathode electrolyte interface (CEI) layer during the cycling. The simulation results of electrochemical resistances, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0005">5c</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a> (Supporting Information), are employed by the models of the equivalent circuit (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0005">5d,e</a>). Notably, the lower values of <i>R</i><sub>sf</sub> for NFM-Sc imply that the thinner thickness of the CEI layer was formed. Moreover, the Sc-modified samples display a much lower increased parameter of <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> from 136.1 to 263.7 Ω, while the pristine from 217.7 Ω increased to 472.8 Ω after 100 cycles, which could be attributed to the interface side reaction and particle microcracking is significantly alleviated due to the enhanced crystal structure stability.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202402398-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/7a22d16b-28b4-46e9-853b-c8b0f92565a0/adfm202402398-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/7a22d16b-28b4-46e9-853b-c8b0f92565a0/adfm202402398-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/212bd791-ad56-4b35-a590-7476b299b40d/adfm202402398-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/7a22d16b-28b4-46e9-853b-c8b0f92565a0/adfm202402398-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202402398-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202402398" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">EIS test results for a) NFM, b) NFM-Sc at different states, and c) fitting results. The corresponding equivalent circuit for d) uncycled and e) after-cycled cathodes. f,g) Linear fitting at the oxidation/reduction peak for CV test. h) The fitting slope at different oxidation/reduction peaks. i,j) the GITT tested curves and calculated Log(<i>D<sub>Na+</sub></i>) in charge/discharge process. k) the comparison for ohmic polarization of the voltage of NFM and NFM-Sc.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To explicitly clarify differences of rate performances, the apparent sodium ion diffusion kinetics was explored by cyclic voltammetry (CV) measurement under various scan rates (0.1, 0.3, 0.5, 0.7, and 0.1&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>) within the potential range of 2.0–4.2&nbsp;V. As seen two pair of redox peaks in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a> (Supporting Information), the better cycling reversibility and less polarization for NFM-Sc, which was well consistent with the dQ/dV plots. On the basis of the Randles–Sevcik equation, the value of D<sub>Na+</sub> mainly has a linear positive correlation with the slope.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0039_R_d169048048e1288" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Sci. China Mater.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The obvious larger slopes for NFM-Sc than NFM, as depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0005">5f–h</a>, suggest the distinctively improved Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics. Besides, galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) measurement results firmly establish the improved sodium ion diffusion kinetics of the NFM-Sc, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0005">5i,j</a>, which presents higher Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients than that of NFM at various voltage ranges. Especially in the voltage area of below ≈3.2&nbsp;V and high voltage of 4.0–4.2&nbsp;V, which corresponds to the periods of two-phase coexistence of the O3-P3 and P3-O3’, indicating the promoted Na<sup>+</sup> transportation capability mainly benefited by suppressing the irreversible phase transformation after introduction of the robust Sc─O bond and extension spacings of Na layers. In addition, it is worth noting that the ohmic polarization values of Sc-modified electrodes were apparent low over the pristine sample, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0005">5k</a>, again manifesting the alleviated electrochemical polarization and providing faster channels for sodium ion migration during the Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation/deintercalation process after Sc-doping.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0040_R_d169048048e1312" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Adv. Energy Mater.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>In order to assess the impact of the Sc doping strategy on the structural stability, several tests, including XRD, XAS, SEM, and XPS, were performed for NFM and NFM-Sc before and after 100 cycles, as depicted in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0006">6</a>. Notably, the noticeably broadened XRD diffraction peaks (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0006">6a</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>, Supporting Information), especially the (006) peak of NFM, whereas the same shape as that of the fresh state for NFM-Sc after cycled, indicating introducing robust Sc─O bond could well-maintained layered structure for long-term cycling. Specifically, the (003) diffraction peak of NFM is considerably left-shifted 0.11°, while no significant variation was observed for NFM-Sc. After calculation, the lattice parameters of NFM underwent substantial shrinkage of 0.016 for <i>a</i> and expansion of 0.0159 for <i>c</i>, which is apparently larger than the changes in NFM-Sc (0.004 and 0.0022), as evidenced in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0006">6b</a>, demonstrating Sc-dopant could effectively mitigate structural degradation. To deeply investigate the coordination environment of electrochemistry active elements Ni and Fe after a cycle by XAS, as depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0006">6c,d</a>. It clearly shows that the larger Ni─O distances and similar Ni-TM distances for NFM-Sc in the R space, which means that the squeezed Ni-O recovered better in the series of Na-O-Ni-O-Na when Na<sup>+</sup> fully intercalated, indicating a more reversible electronic structural. Similar observations happened in the Fe K-edge that longer Fe─O distances in the R spacing for NFM-Sc, which reconfirmed Sc modification could restrain irreversible Fe.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202402398-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/ac8ab15d-18af-42c7-83f1-4418eaf23e96/adfm202402398-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/ac8ab15d-18af-42c7-83f1-4418eaf23e96/adfm202402398-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/38f66b60-4ca0-48af-a017-9a6acff07c26/adfm202402398-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/ac8ab15d-18af-42c7-83f1-4418eaf23e96/adfm202402398-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202402398-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202402398" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) The comparison in the XRD patterns of (003) peak between fresh and after 100 cycled samples, b) corresponding the changes of the lattice parameter. c,d) Ni, Fe K-edge in R spacing for after cycled samples. e–i) SEM images and XPS results of NFM and NFM-Sc electrodes after 100 cycles at 1 C.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>In addition, SEM images revealed that secondary particles of NFM suffered from severe cracks and breakages after cycles due to the severe P3-O3’ phase transitions and anisotropic volume variations that explained its rapid capacity decay. In comparison, the secondary particles of NFM-Sc still maintain the relatively complete spherical shape during prolonged cycling, which greatly benefited from the enhanced structure stability by Sc-modification. Furthermore, the undesirability cycling performance might be attributed to the aggravating parasitic side reactions in the interface areas between bulk surface with electrolyte, where electrolyte salt/solvent decompositions and separation of transition metal usually occur (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information). The C 1s, O 1s, and F 1s of XPS spectra have been designedly analyzed for selected samples after cycling, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0006">6g–i</a>, where the major elements of surface chemical compositions are denoted as CEI. The larger peak area of the C─O and C═O bonds were observed in the C 1s spectrum for NFM, which are assigned to the redundancy byproducts from organic solvents (EC and PC) decomposition during the charge/discharge reaction process. On the other hand, the decreased intensity peaks of C─O and C═O for NFM-Sc, as observed in the O 1s spectrum, again firmly demonstrated the less consumption of cathode-electrolyte and prevented CEI firm growth without limits after Sc modification. More significantly, the reduced peak intensities of the Na─F bond and the disappeared peak of C-F after Sc incorporation, as exhibited in the F 1s spectrum, imply the suppressed dissolution of electrolyte additive FEC and PVDF.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0041_R_d169048048e1372" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>To investigate the influence of Sc infusion on the intrinsic electronic structure of NFM, density functional theory (DFT) calculations were implemented. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0007">7a</a> illustrates the electron localization function (ELF) of oxygen along the (001) plane for both NFM and NFM-Sc. The altered shape of the free electron distribution around oxygen in NFM-Sc indicates the electrostatic attraction of localized electrons near oxygen by Sc<sup>3+</sup>. Comparing the ELF of the transition metal layer (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0007">7b</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a>, Supporting Information), the electron density of Mn/Fe were obviously changed after Sc incorporation, implying the increased lattice oxygen free electron density reinforces the TM─O bonds. Moreover, the differential charge density analysis of selected samples (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0007">7c,d</a>), further evidenced that Sc could provide more charges to the adjacent oxygen atoms and facilitate the electron localization. Furthermore, the density of states (DOS) for NFM and NFM-Sc were calculated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0007">7e</a>, the Sc-doped cathode shifted toward lower energy level, benefiting from the additional electrons provided by Sc atoms, demonstrating the electron localization.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0009_R_d169048048e1400" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Adv. Energy Mater.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The enhanced degree of electronic localization in transition metallic layers is partially attributed to the absence of interacting d orbitals, indicating the formation of an ionic bond between Sc and O.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0042_R_d169048048e1405" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Energy Environm. Sci.">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The O 2p orbital of NFM-Sc exhibits a dominant presence of electronic states near the Fermi level, suggesting facilitation of oxygen redox reactions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0043_R_d169048048e1411" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Energy Environm. Sci.">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Above all, the introduction of Sc<sup>3+</sup> performs a crucial role in achieving higher electron localization, effectively improving oxygen redox reversibility, and enhancing structural stability.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202402398-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/5cf6165d-6259-42ac-917c-d1068637251a/adfm202402398-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/5cf6165d-6259-42ac-917c-d1068637251a/adfm202402398-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/1cc6c103-972e-4e3d-a686-6df86b145839/adfm202402398-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/5cf6165d-6259-42ac-917c-d1068637251a/adfm202402398-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202402398-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202402398" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a,b) The mapping results of the ELF plot for the (0 0 1) plane were obtained for selected samples c,d) The differential charge density of NFM and the NFM-Sc. e) The pDOS for the NFM and the NFM-Sc. f) Schematic diagrams of the structural evolution for NFM and modification mechanism of Sc during long-term cycling.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To summarize, Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202402398-fig-0007">7f</a> vividly demonstrates a more stable structural evolution for NFM via Sc-incorporation, which could effectively adjust interlayer structure, restrain phase lattice transition, and reduce the dissolution of transition metals, ensuring a relatively complete structure during long-term cycling.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202402398-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202402398-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, the high-performance RE-doped NFM layered cathodes are well designed by introducing larger ionic radius and robust RE-O bond in the configuration of O-Na-O-TM-O-Na-O, enabling the shrunk slab of TMO<sub>6</sub> and broadened spacings of Na layers. Simultaneously, a crucial role is played by Sc-dopant in improving the Ni/Fe redox reversibility and alleviating the unfavorable phase transitions of P3-O3’-P3’ combined with restrained irreversible migration of Fe<sup>4+</sup>. As a consequence, the Sc-modified NFM cathode exhibits optimal comprehensive electrochemical performances, especially a high-voltage durability that can be stably operated to a high cutoff charge voltage of 4.2&nbsp;V with an 80.2% capacity retention after 500 cycles at 5 C. This rational regulation strategy proposed in this work may help build practical high-energy SIBs with improved sustainability.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202402398-sec-0040">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202402398-sec-0040-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202402398-sec-0050">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202402398-sec-0060">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202402398-sec-0070">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202402398-sec-0070-title"> Material Synthesis</h4>
                  
                  <p>O3-layered cathode material NaNi<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (NFM) and RE (rare earth)-doped NFM were synthesized via a typical and solid-state calcination method. First, the Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>(OH)<sub>2</sub> precursor was synthesized by a coprecipitation method, which was reported by previous work.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0044_R_d169048048e1491" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - J. Mater. Chem. A">44</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Then wet mixed the hydroxide precursor and Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> (Macklin, AR) with the molar ratio of TM/Na was 1:1.05. Lastly, the mixtures were calcined at 850&nbsp;°C for 15&nbsp;h in the furnace to obtain the NFM sample, then cooled down to room temperature naturally and timely stored in an argon-filled glovebox to minimize the impact of moisture. The same synthesis process with an additional 1.0 mol% rare metal nitrate (Scandium nitrate hexahydrate/ Yttrium nitrate hexahydrate/ lanthanum nitrate hexahydrate, Aladdin, AR) in the mixture process for synthesis RE-doped NFM material.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202402398-sec-0080">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202402398-sec-0080-title"> Materials Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>The actual element ratios were measured by an inductively coupled plasma-optical emission spectrometer (ICP-OES, PerkinElmer-Optima-3000DV, USA). The powder X-ray diffraction (XRD) data were collected over a scan range (2θ) of 10°–80°on an Ultima IV (Rigaku, Japan) with Cu Kα radiation (<i>λ</i> = 1.5405 Å). XRD Rietveld refinement was performed with the FULLPROF program.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202402398-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202402398-bib-0045_R_d169048048e1512" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Acta Crystallograph. a-Found. Adv.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The morphology of the samples was investigated by field-emission scanning electron microscope (FE-SEM, JSM-7610Fplus, JEOL, Japan). The lattice fringes and elemental distribution images were obtained from high-resolution transmission electron microscopy (HR-TEM, FEI Tecnai G2F20, USA). X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS, Thermo Scientific K-alpha, USA) measurements were performed to detect the oxidation state of metal elements, and the results were fitted using Avantage software. The Ni/Fe K-edge were measured at BL11B station in Shanghai Synchrotron Radiation Facility.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202402398-sec-0090">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202402398-sec-0090-title"> Electrochemical Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>The half-cell electrochemical performances were examined using CR2016 coin cells. First, the cathode active material, super P carbon, and polyvinylidene fluoride binder were mixed in N-methyl-1,2-pyrrolidone solvent at a mass ratio of 8:1:1. Then, the mixed slurry was uniformly spread on the Al current collector and dried in a vacuum oven overnight at 120 &nbsp;°C for 12&nbsp;h. The mass loading of active material was ≈2.0–3.0&nbsp;mg cm<sup>−2</sup> for the half cell. Next, the coin cell was assembled in the argon-filled glovebox using a pure Na thin disk as a counter electrode and glass fiber membrane (GF/D, Whatman) as the separator. The electrolyte was used 1.0&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaClO<sub>4</sub> dissolved in PC:EC  =  1:1 solvent with 5 wt.% FEC. For the full cell, using commercial hard carbon (HC) as anode, and a capacity balance of positive: negative electrode of 1:1.1 was used. The Galvanostatic charge–discharge measurements are conducted on a LANHE CT2001A battery test system at room temperature (25 °C). The voltage window was 2.0–4.2&nbsp;V for half-cell tests and 1.5–4.2&nbsp;V for full-cell tests. Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) and cyclic voltammetry (CV) measurements were performed were performed using an Autolab (MULTI AUTOLAB M204) electrochemical workstation. In the galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) experiments, the applied repeated current pulses were determined by considering 0.1 C (12&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>) for 20&nbsp;min followed by a relaxation time of 2&nbsp;h.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202402398-sec-0100">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202402398-sec-0100-title"> Density Functional Theory Calculations</h4>
                  
                  <p>All of the first-principles calculations were performed by using Vienna ab initio simulation package (VASP) within the density. functional theory (DFT) framework. The interactions of electron and ion were described via the projector augmented-wave (PAW) methods. The exchange-correlation interactions of electrons were described with the generalized gradient approximation (GGA) with the Perdew-Burke-Ernzerhof (PBE) version. According to the research before, the Hubbard-type correction U<i><sub>eff</sub></i> (U<i><sub>eff</sub></i> = U – ∫) has been considered with values of 6, 3.5, 4.9, and 4.9&nbsp;eV for the Ni 3d, Sc 3d, Mn 3d, and Fe 3d orbitals, respectively. To fit the electronic wave functions, the plane-wave kinetic energy cutoff was set of 400&nbsp;eV, and the grid of 3 × 3 × 1 was chosen for the gamma centered Monkhorst pack K-point mesh. The atomic positions were fully relaxed until the maximum energy difference and Hellann-Feynman force on atoms, respectively, converged to 105&nbsp;eV and 0.0l eV A<sup>−1</sup>. The density of state (DOS) calculation was smeared by the Gaussian smearing method.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">

                        <span><a class="google-scholar visitable" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DW.%2BLiu%252C%2BD.%2BLi%252C%2BY.%2BLiu%252C%2BD.%2BLuo%252C%2BR.%2BXu%252C%2BRenewables%2B2024%252C%2B2%252C%2B25.&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202402398&amp;doiOfLink=10.31635%2Frenewables.024.202300044&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><span class="openUrl"><a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_2_8_4_1&amp;dbid=16384&amp;doi=&amp;type=refOpenUrl&amp;url=http%3A%2F%2Fimp-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com%2Fopenurl%2F44IMP%2FICL_VU1%3Furl_ver%3DZ39.88-2004%26rft.genre%3Darticle%26rfr_id%3Dinfo%3Asid%2Fwiley%26rft.aufirst%3DW.%26rft.aulast%3DLiu%26rft.aufirst%3DD.%26rft.aulast%3DLi%26rft.aufirst%3DY.%26rft.aulast%3DLiu%26rft.aufirst%3DD.%26rft.aulast%3DLuo%26rft.aufirst%3DR.%26rft.aulast%3DXu%26rft.jtitle%3DRenewables%26rft.date%3D2024%26rft.volume%3D2%26rft.spage%3D25" title="OpenURL Imperial College London" class="sfxLink visitable" target="_blank">Find at Imperial</a></span></div></li>

    window.addEventListener('load', () => {
        document.querySelectorAll('.admin-bar-popup-menu ul li')?.forEach(function (li) {
